Important Foreign Telegrams

Britain and the United States Have a Consistent Attitude on the Far East Issue

Stimson's Purpose of Visiting Europe Achieved

Simon Refutes Rumors of Suppressing China and Aiding Japan

▲ National Society, Geneva, 3rd: Since U.S. Secretary of State Stimson came to Europe and met with British Foreign Secretary MacDonald, League of Nations dignitaries now expect that a more solid understanding can be reached between Britain and the United States on the Manchurian issue. According to previous reports, Stimson felt disappointed with Britain's attitude towards dealing with the Far East. Although Stimson subsequently denied this, according to the Associated Press, American diplomats were indeed quite frustrated by the policies of British Foreign Secretary Simon before. However, since MacDonald came to Geneva to meet with Stimson, Stimson has received quite encouraging assurances from MacDonald. It is said that MacDonald told Stimson that after the outbreak of the Manchurian crisis, Britain's attitude was slightly weak because he was ill. In the future, Britain's actions will be more closely harmonized with the United States. In addition, after Stimson spoke with representatives of the British autonomous territories, he also confirmed that the attitudes and interests of the autonomous territories in the Far East are very similar to those of the United States.

▲ National Society, Washington, 3rd: An Associated Press reporter said that the purpose of U.S. Secretary of State Stimson's trip to Europe was to seek the assistance of European countries in maintaining the Open Door Policy in China and to promote the success of the disarmament conference. It is now said from reliable sources that this purpose has been largely achieved. However, countries such as Britain, France, and Italy are simultaneously unwilling to take any action to avoid offending the Japanese army. Stimson also has a good impression of the determination of European countries to maintain the dignity of treaties in order to preserve China's independence.

▲ Reuters, London, 4th: Labour MP Coquet asked Foreign Secretary Simon in the House of Commons today, saying that the world is now widely rumored that the Foreign Secretary is using his influence to resist China in order to help the Japanese. Is this statement true? The Foreign Secretary turned pale and replied that this statement is purely fictitious. The Foreign Secretary then briefly described the situation of the Geneva Conference, and then described the Sino-Japanese armistice agreement, saying that I am currently waiting for the news of the signing of the Shanghai Agreement, and will report to the House of Commons after receiving it. The Foreign Secretary then said that the armistice agreement stipulates the establishment of a joint committee to monitor the implementation of the agreement, to observe the withdrawal of troops by both sides, and stipulates that the Japanese army occupying the area will transfer to the Chinese police force that entered the area, and the police force will take over as soon as the Japanese army withdraws. The joint committee has the right to urge attention in any aspect where the agreement is not fulfilled. As Mr. Hee Mong said, we hope that the committee's decisions will be unanimous, and the agreement stipulates that decisions can be made by a majority, and the chairman has the right to vote. According to the reply given by Undersecretary of Foreign Affairs Eden in the House of Commons on May 2nd, he denied that the committee could make a decision on the withdrawal of Japanese troops by a majority. The Foreign Secretary's statement today has dispelled doubts.

Moscow Rumors of Tense Russian-Japanese Relations

Japanese Troops Concentrated in Jilin Province Near the Russian Border

Red Army Determined to Resist Any Aggression

▲ Reuters, Moscow, 3rd: Startling rumors of tense Russian-Japanese relations have again been received here from Shenyang. According to reports, Japanese troops are currently concentrated in Jilin Province, which is adjacent to the Russian border from Boli to the Korean border. It is heard that Japanese troops are currently moving from Harbin and Dunhua to Jilin Province. Japanese military aircraft and Japanese troops protecting the Changchun-Jilin Railway have now been transferred to Zhaoh and Boli in Jilin Province. A telegram from Boli stated that the employees' clubs of the Chinese Eastern Railway held meetings on May Day and sent telegrams to the Russian government protesting Japan's provocative actions against Russia.

▲ National Society, Moscow, 4th: It is reported here that Boli, Chita, Haicanwi, and other areas in the Far East held grand celebrations on Labor Day. Thousands of people guaranteed to do their best to defend the Russian border. General Xiang Luqian (i.e. General Galen), commander of the Far Eastern Red Army, has received countless letters and telegrams, all promising to do their best to resist when enemy troops invade the border. Mr. Bai in Boli Bin said that the Red Army is prepared to be able to repel any attacks, and said that we know how to build a socialist economic organization and will not allow anyone to interfere with our great progress. It is also heard that the employees of the Chinese Eastern Railway in northern Manchuria also had enthusiastic celebrations on May Day.

Disarmament Subcommittee Meeting

Issue of Aircraft Restrictions

Heated Debate Between German and French Representatives

Soviet Russia Sends Memorandum to Disarmament Conference

Satirizing Japan's Destruction of Peace in the Far East

Failure to Give People a Guarantee of Abiding by Treaties

▲ National Society, Geneva, 3rd: Although the General Committee of the International Disarmament Conference is currently adjourned indefinitely, the subcommittees are still proceeding as usual, and the debates are extremely fierce. Within the Naval Committee, U.S. representative Shi Huangsheng argued strongly today that aircraft carriers should not be widely eliminated, saying that war experience has shown that aircraft carriers are very valuable in resisting submarine warfare. German representative Baron Rhinbard strongly opposed, insisting that aircraft carriers must be abolished to comply with the Treaty of Versailles. In addition, the newly formed Technical Subcommittee of the Aviation Committee has begun its work today. Its task is to define the basic issues concerning commercial and military aircraft. After the establishment meeting of the subcommittee, German representative Brandenburg submitted a document relating to Germany's proposed abolition of all air force motions. The German representative also proposed that when defining military aircraft, they can be divided into three categories, namely bombers, reconnaissance aircraft, and pursuit aircraft. Subsequently, German and French representatives engaged in a fierce verbal battle. The French representative strongly advocated that commercial aircraft should be treated equally with military aircraft, and proposed that both types be placed under the supervision of the League of Nations. The German representative claimed that France's proposal was due to the extraordinary progress of German commercial aircraft and the ineffectiveness of the Treaty of Versailles, and was an attempt to exploit the power of German commercial aircraft.

▲ National Society, Geneva, 4th: German Disarmament Representative Leader Na Qingni suddenly departed for Berlin today after a long conversation with German Chancellor Bai Luning on the phone. According to the delegation, he was recalled to the country to discuss the current situation in Geneva.

▲ Reuters, Geneva, 3rd: Russia today submitted an important memorandum to the Disarmament Conference, linking the current Far Eastern dispute with the world's disarmament issue, saying that neighbors who destroy international obligations aimed at safeguarding peace and those who wage war without declaration have failed to give people sufficient guarantee of abiding by disarmament conventions.

French Second Round of Voting, Left-Wing Parties Agree to Cooperate

To Engage the Government Party Head-on

▲ Reuters, Paris, 3rd: Helriot's Social Radical Party has decided to challenge the Tae Tieu government in the second round of voting on Sunday. Therefore, in each electoral district, if the Socialist Party has a greater hope of being elected, the candidates of the Social Radical Party will not join the war to avoid dividing the votes of the Socialist Party, so that the Socialist Party can engage the government party head-on and seize the parliamentary seats of Tae Tieu. Of the 615 seats in the House of Representatives, only 261 have been elected. The right-wing party supporting Tae Tieu occupies 131 seats, the opposition party occupies 120 seats, and the remaining seats have yet to be elected in the second round of voting.

▲ Havas, London, 3rd: The London Daily Electric News Report commented on the French election, saying that even if the rulers of France change, France's foreign policy may not change course.

▲ Havas, Berlin, 3rd: German newspapers have made many comments on the French election. The Stock Exchange News said that the opposition forces formed by the Socialist Party and the Radical Socialist Party have increased compared to before, but said that it is still not possible to say that they can catch up with the superior position of the majority parties of Tae Tieu. The Volkszeitung said that if the left-wing parties want to make the Tae Tieu government fail, they must win at least 60 more seats than before. The Local People's Voice said that those who sympathize with the left-wing alliance are inevitably rejoicing too early, because even if the left-wing parties win as they expect, they cannot organize a cabinet.

Former German Foreign Minister to Visit Russia to Investigate Economic and Political Situation

▲ National Society, Berlin, 3rd: Former German Foreign Minister Coutis will go to Soviet Russia in the near future to conduct a large-scale investigation to investigate the economic and political situation in the Soviet Union. However, it is said that this move has no political nature. Mr. Kou is going to investigate as the president of the Eastern European National Research Association.

Ancient Red Indian Chieftain's Remains Discovered in Northern America

▲ Reuters, Washington, 3rd: The remains of an ancient Red Indian chieftain and burial artifacts have recently been discovered on Kodiak Island in northern America. After research by the famous anthropologist Dr. Hertley, it is believed that it is sufficient to recognize that the American Indians originated in the Asian continent, crossed the Bering Strait to the west, and reached the coast of Alaska. Over time, they gradually migrated south and multiplied on the North and South American continents. It is also said that although the three major cultures of the Aster, Indian, and Mies in America were eliminated by white people, examining their relics seems to be transmitted from Asia. Dr. Hertley has two reasons for this view: (1) The remains found on the island are fragmented and incomplete. It has been found that the tribesmen admired their life and ate their flesh in groups on the verge of death, and struck their bones to suck their marrow, hoping to obtain the virtues of the dead. South American Indians once had this custom, so Dr. Hertley said that the ethnic group may be descendants of this chieftain; (2) Both the chieftain's skull eye sockets contained iron ivory, and precious stones were placed in the eyeballs. The Asters and Meiers of America also often did this to the dead. Many ancient attachments have also been excavated on Kodiak Island, the dating of which is difficult to verify, but it seems undoubtedly the oldest relics of mankind in America. Therefore, scientists said that when the distant ancestors of the Indians first migrated to the Americas, they should have taken Kodiak Island as the first stop.

Now, they have not taken active actions for the purpose of their dispatch, greatly losing the true meaning of the investigation. Representatives from seven or eight countries, such as Norway, Spain, and Czechoslovakia, have launched fierce attacks, it is said.

Japanese Newspaper Discusses Russia's Plan to Disrupt All of Manchuria

▲Plan to Bomb All Japanese Cities

Nagoya Shimbun's Harbin dispatch states that after the Japanese army expanded into North Manchuria, Russia's situation suddenly changed. The North Manchurian Committee of the Russian Communist Party, with 250 determined combat volunteer leaders, appointed 20 employees of the Chinese Eastern Railway (CER) to secretly plot to destroy the first Songhua River Railway Bridge on the southern line of the CER on March 29th. On the other hand, on March 2nd, the Russian government ordered the Russian Consul-General in Harbin and the Deputy Director of the CER to withdraw all commercial trade from the area. Meanwhile, the Soviet Russian Combat Volunteer Army, believing that the Japanese army was invading Russian territory, conspired to blow up all institutions and throw North Manchuria into great chaos. They all eagerly tried to implement Lenin's legacy. In particular, the Red Air Force, with its strong morale, encouraged comrades to completely bomb all cities in Japan. Using detailed military maps of Manchuria, Mongolia, and Korea, they attempted to disrupt all of Manchuria. Currently, 80 criminals have been arrested, and a large number of evidence has been seized. It is reported that since January 1st, 2,978 Soviet Russian communists have been active in North Manchuria, extremely resentful of the Japanese army's actions, and the unstable situation is becoming increasingly critical.

Itoda Division of the Japanese Army Arrives in Harbin

▲One of the Three Divisions Being Reinforced

▲The Purpose is to Attack the National Salvation Army on the Harbin-Suifenhe Line

▲Residents in the Zhuhe Area Completely Evacuated

▲Soviet Russia Disrupts North Manchurian Transportation to Restrain Japan

Harbin Dispatch: After the Hirose 10th Division of the Japanese Army arrived here, the Itoda Division stationed in Korea continued to arrive on April 26th and will move towards the area between Yimianpo and Shitoukhezi on the Harbin-Suifenhe section of the Eastern Railway. This is one of the three divisions that the Japanese cabinet decided to reinforce in North Manchuria. The arrival date of the remaining two divisions is yet to be determined. In the future, the military center of gravity will be in Harbin. The Japanese military plan is to first disperse the self-defense army of Li Du and Ding Chao and the National Salvation Army of Wang Delin, and then devote all efforts to dealing with Soviet Russia. Therefore, their military actions are becoming increasingly active. The Murai Brigade stationed in Yimianpo has been advancing eastward since the 25th, using a cavalry battalion to protect armored vehicles, repairing the demolished tracks along the way. By the 27th, it had advanced to Hailin Station. The right to operate the section from Yimianpo to Shitoukhezi has been transferred by the Japanese army to more than 100 Manchurian Railway employees, who are jointly managing it with White Russians, and everything is under the control of the Japanese army, completely breaking away from the control of the Eastern Railway Administration and completely turning the guests into the hosts. When the Japanese army advanced, the National Salvation Army in the Shitoukhezi and Hengdaohezi area did not resist but retreated step by step, abandoning the defense of the railway line, and divided into two branches to bypass the Japanese army. On the morning of the 26th, they crossed Yimianpo and attacked Zhuhe, surrounding two battalions of the Japanese army and launching a fierce attack. The Xi Qia troops stationed locally were notified in advance by the National Salvation Army and retreated to Ashihe. Therefore, the Japanese army was trapped in a heavy encirclement, and more than 300 of the two battalions of over 1,000 men were killed. Later, a regiment of the Japanese army from Yimianpo arrived to provide assistance, and the siege was lifted. However, Zhuhe County and the Ujim River Station of the Eastern Railway were destroyed by artillery fire, and the buildings in the two places were turned into scorched earth. Although the National Salvation Army has retreated, it is not far away. The residents in the Zhuhe area were notified by the National Salvation Army to evacuate completely within a week or so. The Eastern Railway provided special assistance and allowed free transportation of refugees to Harbin. By the 27th, 1,004 refugees had arrived in Harbin. Fearing that the National Salvation Army would cut off their retreat, the Japanese army sent two regiments of Itoda's infantry to Ujim to prepare for defense. Due to the disrupted transportation, passenger and freight trains traveling eastward still only run to Yimianpo. Telecommunications only reach Ujim.

The Japanese military department in Harbin arrested a large number of Red Russians, accusing them all of plotting to disrupt transportation. On the 26th, Yagi, the Japanese advisor to the Special Police Department, announced the Soviet Russian organization of a transportation disruption squad in North Manchuria, with 20 people in each squad, specializing in destroying transportation lines along the Eastern Railway and all related buildings, totaling 20 squads. The leaders are all important employees of the Eastern Railway. The focus of sabotage is the Harbin-Changchun line and the Harbin-Suifenhe line. It is also said that this action is directed by the Soviet Russian Far East Special Military District Command. Although this was released by the Japanese side, the actual situation does seem to be the case. At noon on the 27th, a Japanese plane flew east of Yimianpo for reconnaissance and went missing. The Japanese side believes that this was caused by a Soviet Russian guerrilla attack, resulting in the plane crashing. Currently, the Japanese side has removed its false facade towards Russia and entered into arguments, and a firefight may not be far off.

The Japanese army, totaling 6,000 men, departed from Harbin to Yilan to attack Li Du and Ding Chao. They were traveling on ten ships including the Nanxiang, Sanshui, Yanghu, Mingshan, Fuzhou, Shuangcheng, Faku, Liaoyang, Yizhou, and Hangzhou, along with 25 towed barges and 100 sailboats. The sailboats mostly carried grain and grass, covered with canvas. Some say that the figures tied on the ships are straw men, seemingly wanting to use the story of Cao Cao borrowing arrows with straw boats as a clever tactic to attack Yilan. The three Jiangfang warships of the Northeastern Navy, Lishui, Liji, and Jiangqing, and three motorboats have also been dispatched. Each warship is transporting over 100 Japanese soldiers and several artillery pieces. Sailors on the ships were unwilling to be used by the enemy, and some escaped in advance. Those who were discovered by the Japanese were monitored by soldiers, and they were not separated even during meals. However, when sailing near Laoshantou and Wuhe, many took advantage of the night to jump into the river and swim away. The Japanese then stopped the ship mid-way, returned to Harbin, and sought hundreds of White Russians to supplement the crew. On the 27th, the motorboats carrying Japanese soldiers arrived at Laoshantou east of Harbin and were ambushed by the righteous army from the mountains. One boat was destroyed, and 40 soldiers were drowned. Therefore, the Japanese ships are proceeding with great caution. For example, the first batch that departed on the evening of the 27th, when arriving at Tonghe, because downstream is the Jiangbei shore of Tangyuan, a strategic pass, where more than 1,000 of Ma Zhanshan's troops are stationed, defending the area. The Japanese soldiers did not dare to rush in and could only advance slowly. (April 28th)

Northeastern Regions

Current Situation of the Volunteer Army

— Ke

Special Correspondence from Beiping

Recently, many volunteer armies in various parts of Northeast China have been eliminated, and many have also sprung up. For example, the troops of Jin Dexuan and Shi Anquan were utterly defeated in the SuiZhong campaign. Of the more than 20 commanders appointed by the Northeast People's Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association, only one or two tenths are now able to command their troops. However, upon closer examination, the members of each group are still alive and well, mostly establishing their own banners and seeking other paths. In addition to the formal troops of Ding Chao, Li Du, Ma Zhanshan, Su Bingwen, and Yuan Chonggu, the anti-Japanese forces in the Northeast are becoming more deeply entrenched. Recently, the burning of grain and fodder factories near Shenyang, the cutting of telegraph lines, the Xiaobailong and Gaitianhong in northwestern Tongliao, leading more than 8,000 people, are about to move, constantly destroying transportation. The occupation of various institutions in Tonghua by the volunteer army, and various other activities are too numerous to mention, making the Japanese army exhausted and unable to defend against everything. The members of the other troops are also very sound, and their average strength is comparable. If efforts are made to reorganize them and unite them to resist Japan, it will not be very difficult to recover the lost territories of Northeast China.

Shandong Plans to Reform the Military System

▲Will Increase One Division

A person from Jinan said that Jiang Zhongzheng, Chairman of the Military Affairs Commission, believes that the current military system in our country has four types of divisions: A, B, C, and D, with inconsistent numbers of personnel. Therefore, he plans to adopt economic measures to unify the system, using the division as a unit, with two brigades per division and two regiments per brigade. This method is expected to be implemented soon. Currently, Han Fuqu, Chairman of the Shandong Provincial Government and Commander-in-Chief of the Third Route Army, has five divisions under his command. The 20th Division Commander Sun Tongxuan and the 29th Division Commander Cao Fulin are both Class A divisions, with three brigades each. The 22nd Division Commander Gu Liangmin, the 74th Division Commander Qiao Lizhi, and the 81st Division Commander Zhan Shutang are all Class B divisions, with two brigades each. If reorganized according to the new military system, Gu Liangmin, Qiao Lizhi, and Zhan Shutang are already suitable and will not be changed. However, Sun Tongxuan and Cao Fulin each have one extra brigade. These two extra brigades are just enough to form a new division. Therefore, it will be used to increase one division, without increasing the number of personnel or military pay. It is expected that the central government will also approve it. Recently, Han Fuqu convened important generals to Jinan to discuss the methods for the academic and military subjects examinations of each division and brigade in the summer. The implementation of the new military system was also studied. It is said that the most promising candidates for the commander of the newly added division are Li Hanzhang, the 85th Brigade Commander of the 29th Division stationed in Dezhou, and Rong Guangxing, the 87th Brigade Commander of the 29th Division stationed in Jiaozhou. One will be selected and recommended in the future. After the meeting, the division and brigade commanders have returned to their original defenses on the 30th.

The Process of Wang Jialie's Leadership in Guizhou

▲The Rise and Fall of Wang and Mao's Forces

Guiyang dispatch: The Chairman of the Guizhou Provincial Government has been officially changed to Wang Jialie by the National Government. Among them, Mao's resignation and Wang's succession, on the surface, is based on the recommendation of the former Guizhou Provincial Government Chairman Mao Guangxiang by telegram. Mao's concession has an earlier process. When Zhou Xicheng commanded the Guizhou army, Mao and Wang were both division commanders under Zhou. In terms of ability, Wang was better than Mao, but in terms of personal relations, Zhou was closer to Mao, because Mao was Zhou's brother-in-law. Mao was favored by Zhou, and his power was particularly strong and his support was also broad. Therefore, Mao succeeded as chairman after Zhou's death, and Wang was frustrated, so he led his troops into Hunan and left the province. However, his ambition to return to the province and participate in politics has never been abandoned. When he was in Hunan, he spared no effort in reorganizing the army. Because transportation in Hunan Province is more convenient than in Guizhou, and the replenishment of military supplies is also easier. Mao could not feel at ease, believing that Wang would inevitably return sooner or later. Therefore, he discussed with his subordinates and invited Wang to return to the province to avoid complications. Wang then personally led four regiments to return, but stopped near the provincial capital without advancing. Mao's initial intention was to allow himself to serve as the chairman, commander-in-chief, and training division commander, and to let Wang be the chairman, responsible for civil affairs, while the positions of commander-in-chief and training division commander would still be held by Mao. Therefore, the telegram recommending Wang as chairman was issued immediately. However, at this time, Wang had not yet entered the province, believing that the implementation of civil power in the province still had to be assisted by military force. At this time, due to disputes in opinion, the people in the provincial capital were quite shaken, fearing that it would cause a war. Fortunately, other middle-ground military officers, such as You Guocai, Che Mingyi, and Huang Yanbin, strongly advised Mao to give up everything. Mao, seeing that the general trend was irreversible, gave up both military and civil power. Currently, Mao still lives in the provincial capital, with only a pistol battalion left to protect him. Therefore, although he lives in the same city as Wang, they can coexist peacefully.

Long Xiang, Clerk of the Hankou Municipal Party Headquarters, Executed for Banditry

▲The Wuhan Garrison Headquarters Investigated and Carried Out the Execution by Firing Squad

Hankou dispatch: Long Xiang, a clerk of the Hankou Municipal Party Headquarters, was arrested on March 5th for a banditry case. The Municipal Party Headquarters listed various doubts and sent a letter to the Garrison Headquarters requesting careful handling, saying that Long was from a prominent family in Xiangyang and worked diligently, fearing that there would be injustice. The Garrison Headquarters also listed evidence confirming Long as the principal offender. The case was extremely concerned by the society. Recently, the Garrison Headquarters concluded its interrogation and sentenced Long Xiang to death. He was executed by firing squad in Wuchang on the 3rd. In addition to announcing the crimes, the Garrison Headquarters also issued an order to its subordinates, strictly prohibiting attacks by word of mouth. The proclamation stated: "The case investigation found that on March 4th, the postal and telecommunications inspection office presented three threatening letters from anonymous bandits to Zhou Zhongxuan's home at No. 6 Tianfu Lane in the French Concession, and attached two returned savings passbooks and several disaster relief receipts. The investigation office was immediately dispatched to investigate and arrest the suspects. On the morning of March 5th, according to Zhou's report, the office arrested Liu Shutang, a tea house worker at the Huihua Hotel, who was tricked by bandits into delivering a letter to Zhou's house to extort money. Then, based on the identification of Cai Linxing, another tea house worker at the hotel, the bandit Zhou Zhuxuan, also known as Long Xiang, who personally wrote the above letters in room 34, was arrested. Two official draft letters, a lieutenant quartermaster Long Xiang's symbol, were found in his pocket, and a list written by the bandit and a broken letter were submitted by the hotel. According to Zhou Zhuxuan's confession, a suspect named Yang Yixin was arrested and sent to the department for handling according to the law. The case was immediately handed over to the military law office for trial according to the law, and the progress of the case was reported separately. Subsequently, the Central Executive Committee sent a telegram instructing that Long Xiang's case of fraud and extortion should be handled according to the law. After repeated court hearings, except for Liu Shutang and Yang Yixin, whose criminal suspicion was insufficient and needed further investigation, as for Zhou Zhuxuan, also known as Long Xiang, Cai Linxing, a tea house worker at the Huihua Hotel, testified in court that he was the one who opened the room, closed the door to write the letter, and asked someone to deliver it. After repeated questioning, it remained consistent. The letters of intimidation to Zhou Zhongxuan and the list submitted by the hotel, as well as the drafts personally written by Zhou Zhuxuan found in his pocket, and other letters, were sent to the Hubei Higher Court Prosecutor's Office and various legal groups to appoint responsible representatives for detailed identification. It was determined that the handwriting was the same. According to this testimony, the suspect was indeed a bandit who robbed Zhou Zhongxuan's family property and continued to send letters to intimidate him. The crime was serious. According to the provisions of Articles 1 and 29 of the Provisional Regulations for the Punishment of Bandits, he was sentenced to death, and his civil rights were deprived for life according to Article 57 of the Criminal Law. The instructions from the E Suijing Public Office [Law] No. 208 stated that the presentation and judgment, as well as the entire case file, were all understood. Zhou Zhuxuan, also known as Long Xiang, etc., dared to collude to rob and then extort money, which was extremely illegal. Since human and material evidence has been collected and the investigation is clear, according to the provisions of Articles 1 and 29 of the Provisional Regulations for the Punishment of Bandits, he is sentenced to death, and his civil rights are deprived for life according to Article 57 of the Criminal Law. There is nothing wrong with it. Permission is granted to execute according to the judgment, and the original file will be returned, and the date of execution should be reported for filing. The rest of the bandits should be arrested and investigated. This order," the proclamation stated, "Zhou Zhuxuan, also known as Long Xiang, 30 years old, from Hunan." (May 3rd)

Disaster Victims from Northern Anhui Flock to Bengbu

▲Local Facilities Provide Two Congee Kitchens

▲Over 7,000 People Eat Every Day

Bengbu dispatch: The Huaihe and Sihe areas in northern Anhui have been plagued by bandits for years, and the people's livelihoods are deteriorating. Last summer, they suffered a terrible flood, with wailing everywhere. Coupled with the rampant bandits, robbing and looting, the survivors were unable to make a living. The strong and cunning turned to crime, joining the bandit gangs to make a living by robbery. Women, children, and the elderly could not maintain their lives and fled the disaster areas, begging for food everywhere, hoping to survive. Unexpectedly, since the spring, northern Anhui has suffered another drought, and the seedlings have failed to sprout. Even in high-lying areas where the flood receded earlier, wheat farmers must wait until June to harvest, and rice farmers will not harvest until September or October. During these months when the old and new crops are not yet available, the spring famine is severe, and starvation is intensifying. Refugees are everywhere, which is heartbreaking to witness. Most of the disaster victims in the Huaihe and Sihe areas believe that Bengbu is a convenient location for transportation north and south and by water and land, and it is easier to beg for food. Therefore, they flocked to Bengbu, turning the good city of Bengbu into a place for the disaster victims of northern Anhui to gather. The streets and alleys are full of orphans who are haggard and distressed, supporting the old and carrying the young, begging from door to door, exposed to the wind and dew, which is extremely miserable. Even starved corpses are seen everywhere. According to statistics, there are no less than 10,000 disaster victims. In the past, the local authorities in charge of disaster relief have implemented relief work, but only for the relatively poor households in the city, paying little attention to the homeless refugees begging from door to door because they have no fixed place to go and cannot be tracked. Now, philanthropists Lu Chewu, Peng Zhuoru, Zhu Zhonghua, Li Mutan, Ding Jiuqing, and Huang Gongchen, etc., have donated money to purchase grain and establish congee kitchens, two in total, one in Wangyingzi behind the east railway station and one in Sanjing Street in the west amusement field. Congee tickets are issued in advance, and the time for distributing congee is from 6:00 a.m. to 10:00 a.m. every day. Each person receives a bowl of rice congee every day, which is just enough to survive. Congee tickets are changed every day, and newcomers can apply for them. In recent days, the east kitchen has cooked eight pots of congee every day, with more than 3,800 people eating, and the west kitchen has cooked six pots of congee every day, with more than 3,200 people eating. According to statistics, more than 7,000 refugees go to the two congee kitchens every day to eat. We hope that philanthropists will quickly raise funds for fundamental relief measures. (May 1st)

Local News

▲ Xu Yabo's Appeal to Jiangsu: Xu Yabo, former district chief of the Water Police, along with the ringleaders Taibao Ashu and Li Wenjun, who had already been executed for conspiring in Shanghai, were major criminals involved in disturbing various coastal counties in Jiangsu and Zhejiang. Xu Pucheng, the first district chief of the Water Police, personally apprehended them in Shanghai, in conjunction with the concession police. Apart from Li Wenjun and others, who were directly escorted to the Zhenjiang Security Office for interrogation and execution, Xu Yabo's name came up because among the stolen goods in the Chenjiahang Qian Boming robbery case in this county, there was a bank deposit book. Xu Yabo had sent someone to the bank to collect the money, but it was confiscated. Qian Boming, the victim, discovered the whereabouts of the stolen goods and filed a lawsuit in court. The case was transferred to the Shanghai Special District Court, and Xu was brought to Songjiang for trial. After several investigations, Li Hui, (also known as Li Wenjun's mistress), was summoned and testified that Taibao Ashu was introduced by Xu Huoquan to become Xu Yabo's disciple. The robbery of Qian Boming's home in Chenjiahang was initiated by Li Wenjun, who informed Xu Yabo at the Changchang Inn, stating that the stolen goods would be used to rescue his disciple Tang Yixin. However, Xu Yabo insisted that the teacher Taibao Ashu had拜, was a mistaken 徐亚伯 (another similar name), and stated that he did not know who had put the deposit book in the mailbox, and it was picked up by a servant. Lawyers Yuan and Liu were present and witnessed this. After repeated defenses, and with legal defenses provided by lawyers Xu Heling, Wang Zengxi, and Lu Longxiang, the county court sentenced Xu Yabo to seven years in prison for robbery on January 23rd of this year. Xu declared his dissatisfaction in court and was detained in the detention center. Now, the appeal hearing has been scheduled, and the court specially dispatched bailiffs yesterday (the 3rd) at 3 pm to escort Xu to Jiangsu for the hearing.

▲ Water Police Recover Kidnapped Victims: After two farmers, Gao Liansheng and Gao Lianfa, from the Qianyue Town of Jiashan under the jurisdiction of the Jiaxing Water Police Second District, were kidnapped in late March, the district strictly ordered its subordinates to investigate the case and rescue the hostages. Now, the bandits in the case sent a letter to the hostage's family to negotiate the ransom in Shanghai. Police detectives successively arrested Yan Baoshu, Lu Aqing, Hang A'er, Pan Tingfang, Wang Lianfu, Wang Jisheng, and women Yan Lu and Hang Zhou, a total of eight people, and escorted them to the First Special District Court for interrogation and detention. Upon learning of this, the Water Police District immediately went to Shanghai to bring the eight bandits back to Jiaxing for interrogation. They have now confessed to the location where the hostages were held. The police immediately escorted the criminals to Zhang A'da's house in Yunjucun Zhangjiaqiao, Xinqi, and rescued the two hostages, Gao Liansheng and Gao Lianfa. They also arrested the bandits Li Maolin and Wang A'san, who were guarding the hostages. The case will now be transferred by the district to the court for further investigation.

▲ Starving People Block River Workers' Relief Wheat: A dispatch from Nantong states that the Jiangchuan River in the Jinghua District of Nantong was decided to be dredged by the Water Conservancy Conference, using labor as a form of relief. On the 3rd, a large quantity of relief wheat was transported from the city. However, when the wheat boats arrived at Tangfangtou, they were suddenly blocked and looted by five or six hundred starving men and women. They also resisted and injured Cai Xianglin, the head of the defense corps. Upon receiving the report, the county government immediately dispatched the county police team to suppress the situation.

▲ Zhang Jian's Property Sold to Aid Relief: A dispatch from Nantong states that Zhang Jian's property, after being returned by the provincial government, is now being voluntarily allocated by Zhang to the Jiangbei disaster area as funds for dredging rivers and repairing dikes. Various real estate properties in Nantong are currently being sold at auction.

▲ Headquarters Executes Key Criminal: A letter from Qingjiang states that Zhou Xiangting from Dongtusheng, Funing County, once served as a member of the Jiangsu Provincial Assembly during the warlord era. In 1929, he was appointed as a fake brigade commander by Ma Yuren, gathering a thousand bandits and occupying the Caiqiao area of the county, committing adultery, looting, and all kinds of atrocities. In January 1930, he led bandits to rob the Huacheng Salt Reclamation Company. In July of the same year, he held up the manager and more than ten other employees of Huacheng, extorting 60,000 yuan in foreign currency. The Funing County Government reported the case to the Provincial Government, which resolved to issue an arrest warrant at the 265th meeting. Last winter, the criminal secretly came to Huaiyin to engage in subversive activities and was caught by the 25th Route Army Headquarters. After the headquarters summoned the victims to conduct questioning, it was confirmed that he was a major bandit in the Yancheng and Funing counties of Jiangbei. He was sentenced to death and executed by shooting at the Qingyang Small Railway Station today after the headquarters verified his identity.

▲ Arrests Made for Eating Sparrow Rice: Liu Yongkui, the leader of the 4th squad stationed in Xiyan Village under the 2nd squad of the Rugao County Police, received a report on the 28th from Sun Zhanshu, a resident of Huangbaihu, stating that several people were causing trouble at his home. Upon receiving the report, the squad leader immediately dispatched a team to surround and suppress the situation, resulting in a conflict. Huang Shengshu, Huang Shengmi, Huang Shengshou, Huang Shengying, Feng Caicheng, Ding Wang, Liu Kejiu and others were arrested on the spot. One police officer, Chen Jinquan, was injured and later died. Later, Huang Zizhan and Huang Liuzhanger were also apprehended and sent to the brigade headquarters for investigation. However, it was later heard that Huang Shengmi and others were members of a sparrow association, and this time they were begging for contributions.

57925, 58226, 58267, 58388, 58394, 58425, 58489, 58667, 58810, 59147, 59154, 59346

Case of Japanese Soldiers Crossing a Bridge and Stabbing Seven Chinese

▲The Municipal Council Bears Responsibility

▲The Municipal Government Seriously Negotiates

▲The Chinese Ratepayers' Association Offers a Solemn Admonition

▲American Officials Hope for a Swift Resolution

At half past six in the afternoon the day before yesterday, Japanese soldiers near the Wuzhen Road Bridge stabbed seven Chinese people, creating an extremely serious situation for a time. Later, officers dispatched by the concession police went to suppress the incident, and two American soldiers assisted in dissuading the perpetrators. The Japanese soldiers who committed the assault then retreated to Zhabei. This case is of great importance and has garnered much attention from all sectors. Details are as follows:

▲Protest from the Municipal Government: Yesterday, the Shanghai Municipal Government sent a letter to the Municipal Council, stating: "To the Secretary-General of the Shanghai Municipal Council: On the afternoon of the 3rd of this month, near the Wuzhen Road Bridge on Xin Zha Road, Japanese soldiers crossed into the concession, chased pedestrians, and reached Park Road, stabbing seven Chinese people. This case has already been reported to your council by the responsible police station. As the incident location is within the concession, your council is responsible for ensuring the safety of Chinese residents within the special zone. However, your council was neither able to prevent nor stop the violent behavior of the Japanese soldiers within the concession, causing our people to suffer greatly. We express our deep regret. We hereby send this letter to request that you investigate, conduct serious negotiations, and instruct your subordinates to make every effort to protect Chinese residents within the concession, so that similar incidents do not occur again. We hope for a prompt response to maintain our public friendship. Sincerely, Yu Hongjun, Secretary-General."

▲Admonition from the Chinese Ratepayers' Association: The Chinese Ratepayers' Association of the Public Concession, concerned about the repeated incidents caused by Japanese soldiers in the concession in recent days, causing residents to feel insecure, sent another letter to the Municipal Council yesterday, requesting that effective measures be taken quickly to restore normalcy as soon as possible. The original letter stated: "To the Secretary-General: On the 3rd of this month, our association requested your council to quickly investigate and rescue the twenty-five employees of the Nanyang Printing Company at 322-323 Tiantong Road who were kidnapped by Japanese soldiers and whose whereabouts are unknown, and to adopt the most effective measures to restore normalcy as soon as possible. On the same day, we also received a letter from Yu Hede, Chairman of the Ningbo Native Place Association in Shanghai, regarding the same matter. Unexpectedly, today's newspaper reported that on the afternoon of the 3rd, Japanese soldiers again used bayonets to stab pedestrians on Xin Zha Road, and attacked an old woman in the Li Hengxing Yuanyuan Shop near Jiangyuan Lane for no reason. They also provoked trouble at the Xiangtai Clothing Store nearby. When they failed, they turned to Wang Fengtai Foreign Goods Store and used knives to smash glass cabinets and counters. We were shocked and dismayed upon reading this. For a month, your council has been striving to restore normalcy, and based on this desire, you even listened to one-sided reports and issued a statement through your council's intelligence office, tolerating and exhorting the Chinese. However, the Japanese soldiers' violent acts in the concession in recent days show that your council no longer has the authority to maintain order in your mind. It is clear that they will use such violent means to achieve some purpose. If this continues, it will inevitably cause the residents of the concession to have an intolerable mentality, suspecting your council's ability to prevent disturbances and restore normalcy. The impact of this is immeasurable. Our association hereby solemnly admonishes you to pay attention to the seriousness of this situation, quickly adopt effective measures of restraint, and fulfill the so-called fair treatment obligations of a fair agency, to ensure that similar incidents do not occur again, so that residents can live and work in peace. We eagerly await your prompt reply regarding the handling of this matter."

▲Report from the North-China Daily News: The North-China Daily News reported: "Yesterday evening (the 3rd) at 6:30 PM, approximately sixty or seventy Japanese marines left their defense posts and crossed the Wuzhen Road Bridge, entering the Xin Zha area. It is said that their purpose was to punish several Chinese who threw stones at Japanese sentries across the Suzhou Creek in the afternoon. Although this matter was temporarily resolved peacefully on the spot, negotiations are expected to follow. It is reported that at least ten Chinese were injured by bayonets and rifle butts, three of whom spent the night at the Baolong Hospital. Initially, a Chinese police officer on duty saw Japanese soldiers climbing over the iron gate and quickly telephoned the police station. Before the police station received the call, the head constable had dispersed police teams at Wuzhen Road and the intersecting roads. After the Japanese soldiers crossed the bridge, they arbitrarily stabbed and beat Chinese people and shopkeepers on the road with bayonets and rifle butts. They continued to advance while attacking, eventually reaching the corner of Xin Zha Road and Meibaige Road. The head constable Fei Liepu and deputy head constable Lin, leading Chinese and Indian police officers, happened to arrive at the scene and saw Japanese soldiers attacking Chinese people on Xin Zha Road. The other Chinese people fled in panic and closed their shop doors. The police team then saw several Japanese soldiers on Wuzhen Road trying to drag a Chinese man with bayonet wounds across the bridge into the Zhabei area. The Chinese man struggled desperately and shouted for help. Head Constable Fei Liepu immediately stepped forward to intervene, stating that if they wanted to detain the Chinese man, they should do so through the appropriate authorities and report to the Xin Zha police station. The Japanese soldiers were furious and wanted to make trouble for Fei and Deputy Head Constable Lin. At this time, the Japanese soldiers chased after a Chinese man who was watching from the side. The Chinese man quickly hid behind Fei. The Xin Zha Road area was filled with noise and commotion. The Japanese soldiers then tried to detain a Chinese civilian on Park Road. When the Chinese detective who arrived in a police car was forcibly dragged across the bridge, he was also stopped by a police officer. However, the Japanese soldiers stubbornly refused to comply. Subsequently, a Japanese military officer who could speak English ordered the Japanese soldiers to stop. Many Japanese soldiers then returned to Zhabei. Within a minute or two, U.S. Army Major Quilo arrived with a team. Quilo then spoke with the Japanese military officer. The Japanese military officer stated that two Chinese police officers witnessed Chinese people throwing stones and did not intervene. He also demanded that Major Quilo guarantee that such actions would not occur again; otherwise, the Japanese soldiers would enter the concession again to take appropriate countermeasures. While the two were talking at length, several Japanese soldiers sneaked behind the American soldiers' team and tried to detain the Chinese detective they had previously failed to detain. Detective Peng Lait saw this and shielded him with his body, thus preventing the detention."

▲Report from the Shanghai Evening Post & Mercury: The Shanghai Evening Post & Mercury reported: "Last night, seventy or eighty Japanese sailors left their posts in Zhabei, climbed over the iron gate and barbed wire on Wuzhen Road, and stabbed or beat Chinese people in the Xin Zha area with guns. Later, U.S. Army Major Quilo, accompanied by a platoon of American soldiers and the head constable of the Municipal Council police, firmly intervened, and the Japanese soldiers retreated to Zhabei. Currently, the Municipal Council and the consuls of the countries concerned have not taken any formal action regarding this matter, but it is believed that the authorities will present negotiations after obtaining a detailed report on the fact that the Japanese soldiers stationed in Zhabei entered the Public Concession without permission."

▲Opinions from American Officials: A Washington dispatch from the Guomin News Agency on the 3rd stated: "Today, the U.S. Department of War and the State Department have not yet received official reports regarding the incident in Shanghai, south of the Suzhou Creek, where Japanese soldiers and American soldiers nearly clashed. However, officials, based on reports in newspaper dispatches, expressed the opinion that they believe the American soldiers acted according to their duties and hope that this matter can be resolved quickly and smoothly on the spot."

True Cholera Discovered in Shanghai

▲Occurring Earlier Than Ever Before

A doctor from the Shanghai Epidemic Hospital at 545 Xizang Road reported that the hospital has been open for more than ten years, and it has never seen cholera cases occur so early. Now, patients with true cholera have been admitted to the hospital for saline injections for several days in a row. It is hoped that citizens who have not contracted the disease will strictly avoid eating raw, cold, and unclean foods. Those who have contracted the disease should go to the hospital for treatment as soon as possible, day or night. It is also reported that the hospital has set up a special department to prevent the spread of cholera, specializing in cholera prevention serum injections. The injection time is from 2:00 PM to 4:00 PM every day, and it is free of charge.

Yu Youren's Doubts Regarding Sun Ke's Talk

▲Abandoning Tutelage and the Crisis of the Chinese Revolution

Mr. Yu Youren recently published a long article, which is excerpted below:

In the current situation of China, to still trace back to the past of the revolution is already a very tragic matter. The main force of the revolution is gradually declining, the leadership of the revolution is increasingly shaking, and even the object of the revolution and the beliefs and will of the revolutionaries are becoming increasingly blurred. If we admit that the Chinese revolution has not been completed, then we cannot destroy the party and claim it is a remedy. Recently, those responsible within the party, often due to the severity of the national crisis and facing accusations from the outside world, advocate for a hasty constitutional government, sacrificing themselves to please others. We are heartbroken by the national crisis and dare not agree with them, so we express our doubts to question the wise. The arguments recently published by Comrade Zhesheng, as recorded in various newspapers, unintentionally fall into serious errors. When the national crisis first arose, we pointed out that various parties had this tendency to destroy the party to save the country, and we strongly argued that if the party is destroyed, the country cannot be saved in the end. Now, unfortunately, Zhesheng's words are so easily exploited by others. Summarizing his arguments, one point is that the current central government cannot lead the national masses, which is undeniable. Another point is that the party's credibility has been completely lost, and if we want to remedy this, we must have the determination to reform thoroughly. We truly do not know how these affirmed premises are established. Does it mean that the current party's regime cannot lead the national masses? If so, then where is the one who can lead? Is it the Communist Party? Is it the Nationalist faction? Is it the re-emergence of warlords and bureaucrats? Any revolutionary party or political movement that can obtain revolutionary leadership and a certain form of regime must have its historical background and the sure conditions of society, which cannot be achieved by fantasy. Nor can it be achieved by unwarranted self-deprecation. The party's ability to lead the Chinese national revolution is naturally based on the determination of objective facts. The Communist Party's method of transcending the economic stage cannot be pushed forward, and the Nationalist faction's method of representing a narrow national viewpoint and guild economic ideas cannot be pulled back. If it is said to be the warlords and bureaucrats, then can these remnants of the era and dregs of the revolution emerge from the tombs and take over the regime? Is there such a reason? If it is said that the people should govern themselves through constitutional government, then after the Republic of China, the Republic has been destroyed several times, and even the law has disappeared without a trace. If there was no revolutionary party persevering, then what is called the Republic of China today would have long been impossible to ask about. Since Zhesheng has the above affirmation, he advocates preparing for the implementation of constitutional government, believing that the period of tutelage has been four years, merely in name, with no effect to speak of. If this continues, time will not wait for us, so he advocates starting preparations for constitutional government quickly, without waiting for the end of the tutelage. Moreover, the unfinished work of local self-government can be carried out simultaneously after the start of constitutional government, without waiting for its completion. He also said that resistance to Japan cannot be achieved by the government's individual strength today, but only through cooperation between the government and the people can the final result be achieved. Once constitutional government is established, the government and the people will be united, and the strength of resistance to Japan will naturally be strong, etc. Since we know the sequential relationship between tutelage and constitutional government, with the start of constitutional government dependent on the completion of tutelage, how can tutelage be ended prematurely and constitutional government suddenly appear? Did the Republic of China not have a provisional constitution? Its essence was equal to a constitution. There was indeed a constitutional political system. The restoration of the imperial system was like a fox burying its prey, only to have another fox dig it up. Later, Cao Kun used bribery to become president, and the yellow satin constitution displayed at Tiananmen Square still remains in history, still flowing with residual filth. The constitution was in place, and constitutional government was implemented, but where was the Republic of China that was sought through revolution? Now, once again, the old things are brought up, with the clamorous voices of the crowd, eagerly as if they cannot wait, being the same people who legislate to destroy the law and govern to ruin governance. All constitutional governments come from revolution, and there has never been anyone who does not vow to carry out revolutionary doctrines but can immediately implement the rule of law. Those people did not completely crush the revolutionary party members in the past, exterminated the seeds of revolution, and on one hand, they echoed the imperial system, the restoration, and bribery. Later, they came to echo party rule, but ultimately disliked its inconvenience, and so today they think of a way to remove its foundation. The so-called ending of tutelage is ending the party's leadership of the revolution, lightly masking its traces with the beautiful name of constitutional government. In addition, there are so-called transcendent scholars and famous figures in the opposition, all echoing constitutional government, praising it to the skies. Their ambitions are admirable, but their actions are often mistaken. Under revolutionary politics, there is no such thing as transcendence; in a revolutionary environment, there is no such thing as being in the opposition. If they all exercise the four powers, they have already controlled the governing tools. If they must borrow other means to seek so-called constitutional government, they will appropriately open their arms to the counter-revolutionary groups, which is regrettable. This is still speaking in terms of personnel. As for constitutional government itself, the hasty creation of the Republic of China caused the Premier to feel extremely regretful for not first implementing tutelage. Like building a building, it is necessary to have a solid foundation, so that military governance has just ended, and constitutional government has already begun. If this method of crossing a bridge can be effective, then there would not have been successive disturbances after the Republic of China, and the National Founding Program would not have required the Premier to create a system. It is unexpected that Zhesheng would have uniquely lost this teaching in the family. If self-government is not completed, then tutelage is an empty shell; if tutelage is not experienced, then constitutional government is a mere formality. All the past efforts and sacrifices of the Kuomintang were first to obtain tutelage in order to create a revolutionary constitutional government. If only the articles of the constitution and the government organization are considered constitutional government, then the democratic movement of the bourgeoisie is certainly capable of it, and to say that this can unite the government and the people is simply deceiving the masses. As for saying that local self-government can be carried out simultaneously after the start of constitutional government, we truly do not know why the root is abandoned in favor of pursuing the branches. Now, taking the will of a few people as golden rules and jade laws, destroying the Premier's doctrines to destroy the party and destroy the government, this is removing the weapons for the counter-revolutionary groups. How can it be seen as possible? Moreover, tutelage is to use the Premier's doctrines to provide tutelage. We are the Premier's followers and servants of the people. If the task is not done well, we should condemn ourselves before the Premier and the people, and there is no way to change the Premier's teachings. Otherwise, we should not cause disturbances that increasingly trap the country in lawlessness. Therefore, under this meaning, the sincere unity within the party and the people's joint efforts to overcome difficulties are the only key to solving the national crisis and the only path to overcoming the national crisis. Now, desperately seeking a path in all directions, how can there be a proper one? Only by being truly able to unite and make joint efforts, holding on with a strong and persistent heart, can we defend ourselves and resist insults, and not worry about having no methods. Even if there is a national crisis, there is nothing to fear. Therefore, on the part of the party members, they must carefully choose how to conduct themselves, diligently encourage courage, be the vanguard of the people, and never forget the responsibility of building and governing the country. On the part of the people, they should also supervise the party and the government from a positive perspective, so that they will fight without surrendering or losing rights, and concentrate their efforts on the common path. If this is the case, then the whole country will be truly united, and we will surely be able to resolve the national crisis and promote the success of the revolution in the shortest possible time. May 3, 1932."

Yan Yutang Kidnapped

▲This is the Second Time

▲He Has No Savings

Yan Yutang, a local, 53 years old, residing at 1 Pingliang Road, Yangshupu, left home yesterday morning around 8:30 AM in his own car, number 8967, to go to the Guangyu Business Company at 58 Jiangxi Road to handle business. When the car arrived at the entrance of number 58, it stopped abruptly. As Yan was about to get out of the car, three thugs suddenly jumped out from the roadside, all holding weapons. Two bandits helped Yan back into the car, and one bandit opened the door, got into the driver's seat, and threatened the driver, Gao Asi, with a pistol to drive at full speed towards the south. When they reached the Avenue Edward VII intersection, the bandits pushed Gao out of the car, then turned the steering wheel themselves and sped off to the west. Afterwards, the driver reported to the police station and requested an investigation, but there was no progress to be reported at the time. Yan had been kidnapped once before in the spring of the previous year on Huade Road. At that time, he was sitting in a chartered car and was shot in the left foot by the bandits. His Guangyu Business Company manages the products of the Zhabei Dalong Iron Factory and the Suzhou Sulun Textile Factory, so Yan holds three positions in one person. However, because he came from a humble background, he is extremely frugal and has been enthusiastic about social welfare throughout his life, running three voluntary schools. It is said that he only has a business and no savings. He goes to the company to handle business every morning, entering and leaving alone, without hiring bodyguards. He has six sons, who are divided into Sulun, Dalong, and Guangyu services. The remaining two sons are still studying, with one studying in the United States and one in the country. It is also reported that the car number 8967 was found in western Shanghai last night.

Old Goods Store Privately Purchases Large Amount of Gunpowder

▲ Weighing 230 Pounds

▲ Accomplices Attempt to Profit

▲ Detected and Arrested by Police

▲ Court Has Already Conducted Preliminary Hearing

The "Gonghexing" old goods store, located at 864 Beijing Road and owned by He Chenpu, had recently purchased a substantial quantity of gunpowder from places like Datong, weighing a total of 230 pounds. At approximately 8:00 AM the day before yesterday, the gunpowder was divided and loaded into three burlap sacks, with old copper and scrap iron mixed in to conceal it. They hired a rickshaw puller, Qian Xiaosanzi from Jiangbei, and Li Haidao, with his rickshaw, intending to transport the goods to a certain fireworks shop in the Hongqiao area of the West Gate. As the rickshaw passed through Xizang Road, they were suddenly stopped by four detectives: Miao Baosheng (nicknamed "Little Guangdong") from Changzhou, and Lu Bosheng, a local. They suspected that the rickshaw was carrying explosive gunpowder and violating the law, so they ordered the rickshaw to stop and forcibly transported it to 277 Huile Lane, Yunnan Road, for storage. At the same time, Qian and Li were taken to the Qingliange teahouse on Fuzhou Road and held captive, intending to make a move. However, the plan was not kept secret, and the Laozha Police Station learned of it. They dispatched Western Inspector Howell, Chinese detectives Yang Xinzheng and Lang Zuyin to Huile Lane, where they seized the gunpowder. They then went to the Qingliange teahouse and arrested Qian Xiaosanzi and Li Haidao. Subsequently, they proceeded to the Gonghexing old goods store on Beijing Road and arrested two shop assistants, Wang Guiqing from Suzhou and Fang Chunquan. The store owner, He Chenpu, was not arrested because he happened to be in Datong. Later, Lu Bosheng was arrested on Ningbo Road and taken into custody. Soon after, Miao Baosheng also surrendered himself to the police station. They were separately detained. Yesterday morning, they were all transferred to the First Special District Court, Criminal Division One. The police lawyer, Qian Xunjiu, stood up and presented the case, stating that the police are prosecuting Qian, Li, Wang, and Fang under Articles 44 (accomplice) and 201 (public endangerment) of the criminal law. Miao and Lu are being prosecuted under Article 316 (obstruction of freedom) of the criminal law, etc. According to the statements of the Chinese and Western detectives, Qian Xiaosanzi and Li Haidao confessed that they were hired by Wang and Fang to transport the sacks to Hongqiao. At the time, they only knew that the contents were old copper. As the rickshaw passed through Xizang Road, Miao and Lu stopped them and dragged the rickshaw into Huile Lane on Yunnan Road. At the same time, they were taken to the Qingliange teahouse and guarded by Lu. Later, detectives arrived and took them to the police station. Wang and Fang claimed that the gunpowder was purchased by the store owner and that they were delivering it to a fireworks shop yesterday, etc. Miao Baosheng testified that yesterday morning, he encountered Lu Bosheng and a rickshaw on Xizang Road. Lu told him that the rickshaw was carrying contraband gunpowder and instructed him to quickly telegraph Inspector Wang Changgen of the General Police Station. He then hired a rickshaw to go to a nearby location to make a phone call. At that time, Inspector Wang was not there, so he returned to Yunnan Road, but the people and goods were gone, saying they had been taken away by the police. He then surrendered himself to the police station, etc. Lu Bosheng confessed that yesterday, he was informed by a Mr. Jiang that Qian's rickshaw was carrying gunpowder, so he stopped them. He admitted to reporting to Inspector Wang. The defendants' lawyers, Fan Gangtao and Wu Zhi, requested bail for the defendants. Judge Qian Hongye reviewed the testimonies and ordered the case to be postponed for seven days for further questioning. Qian Xiaosanzi and Li Haidao were released on bail, while Wang Guiqing and Fang Chunquan were released on a 500-yuan surety from their shop. Miao Baosheng and Lu Bosheng were detained.

Social Affairs Bureau Investigates Losses of Cooperative Societies in War Zone

The cooperative societies in this city are known to be well-developed, with a large number located in the Zhabei, Jiangwan, and Wusong areas. Since the outbreak of the Shanghai Incident, the cooperative societies in the war zone have suffered significant losses due to the war, which caused the dispersion of members and the suspension of operations. For months, the losses have been substantial. In order to thoroughly understand the exact amount of war-related losses suffered by each cooperative society, the Social Affairs Bureau has specially created a survey form and is beginning the investigation. However, since the addresses of many cooperative societies in the war zone have changed, and the forms cannot be delivered, all cooperative societies are requested to promptly and voluntarily come to the bureau to obtain and fill out the forms for statistical compilation.

Reasons for Closure of Banque Belge pour l'Étranger in Peiping

The branch of the Banque Belge pour l'Étranger (Belgian Bank for Foreign Affairs) established in Peiping was originally dedicated to negotiating railway matters with the government. Now that the government has moved south and commerce in Beijing is gradually declining, the head office in Brussels sees no need to maintain the branch, so it has ordered the branch to close at the end of this year. In recent years, all matters related to negotiating with the government have been handled by the Shanghai branch of the Banque Belge pour l'Étranger, which is more convenient.

According to the Continental Daily News, it was learned yesterday (2nd) that the Shanghai branch of the Banque Belge pour l'Étranger has received instructions from its head office in Brussels to temporarily suspend operations from July 1st. All depositors and holders of the bank's banknotes are requested to withdraw their money or redeem their banknotes before July 1st. Regarding the banknotes, the Citibank is being consulted to handle the redemption after July 1st. The reason for the bank's decision to temporarily suspend operations is clearly due to the commercial stagnation after the Japanese occupation of Shenyang and the invasion of Zhabei, which caused the bank's business to plummet and made it difficult to recover.

Ruihe Company Manufactures High-Quality Domestic Crucibles

The Shanghai Citizens' Association for the Promotion of Domestic Goods has repeatedly received letters and telegrams from factories manufacturing glass, enamel, batteries, and other products, inquiring about the production of domestic crucibles. The investigation department of the association has found that the Xiaoshadu Ruihe Brick and Tile Company produces such crucibles, which are of excellent quality and superior to foreign products. According to the person in charge of the company, crucibles are essential for melting glass materials, enamelware, and electric light bulbs, and have traditionally been imported. In order to promote domestic production and recover lost revenue, the company initiated manufacturing, and has received awards from the Ministry of Industry and Commerce's National Goods Exhibition and other organizations. However, due to the pressure of raw material costs, sales declined, and production was suspended. Now, with the deepening of national crisis, public resentment is growing, and everyone is determined to reject foreign goods. In response to the urging and needs of factories nationwide, the company is expanding its scale and resuming manufacturing. They have hired Mr. Guo Yongkang, a specialist in overseas Chinese industry, to meticulously plan and manage engineering work, and have recruited patriotic workers who left foreign factories to work together and intensify research. The results are excellent, surpassing foreign products in quality. Production is abundant, sufficient to meet the needs of factories nationwide. In order to encourage the production of new domestic raw materials, the association has sent letters to various factories encouraging promotion and sales, and has submitted a request to the Ministry of Industry for a patent to promote the craft.

Tan Meiying Files for Divorce for the Second Time

▲ Zhao Guangzu Did Not Appear in Court Yesterday

▲ Rescheduled for Further Hearing on the 16th

Zhao Guangzu was once infatuated with prostitutes and formed an inextricable bond with the prostitute Mei Fei. He secretly took the deeds of his house and land and gave them to Mei Fei for safekeeping. The prostitute colluded with Hu San and privately mortgaged them. Zhao Lou Tan Meiying later learned of this and filed a lawsuit against Mei Fei and others for embezzlement, which has been accepted and concluded by the court. She also filed a civil lawsuit against Zhao for abandonment, requesting a divorce. After the court summoned and questioned her, it found that the plaintiff's reasons were insufficient and dismissed the case. At the time, Ms. Tan was very dissatisfied and declared an appeal. Subsequently, through the mediation of friends from both sides, Zhao also deeply regretted his actions and accepted all the conditions proposed by Ms. Tan, including abstaining from prostitution. Therefore, Ms. Tan withdrew the appeal and renewed the vows of lifelong companionship. Unexpectedly, not long after, Zhao Guangzu relapsed and became involved with a dancer, Hu A-liu, at a certain dance hall. From then on, Zhao and Tan fell out again. Zhao did not continue to fulfill the terms of the previous agreement. Ms. Tan was abandoned and hired lawyer Jiang Yiping at the end of last year to sue Zhao for abandonment in the First Special District Court. The complaint has already been published in the newspapers, so I will not repeat it here. Yesterday afternoon was the date for the court hearing. The plaintiff, Tan Meiying, and lawyer Jiang arrived on time. Ms. Tan's charm remained as before, but the defendant, Zhao Guangzu, did not appear in court and only sent lawyer He as a representative. He stated that all the plaintiff's allegations lacked supporting evidence and were unreliable. Moreover, before marriage, the plaintiff studied at school, and the tuition fees were all paid by the defendant. All the expenses for the woman's side at the time of marriage, as well as the dowry fee, were also paid by the defendant. The defendant's treatment of the plaintiff can be said to be benevolent and righteous. Although the plaintiff has filed for divorce again, the defendant still hopes that the plaintiff can repent and return soon to maintain the family's happiness. The judge instructed that the parties should appear in person to express their intentions, so he ordered that the hearing be postponed to the afternoon of May 16th to summon the defendant to court for questioning.

Negotiations Initiated Over Dismissal of Teacher at Peicheng Girls' School

▲ Mediation Once Failed

Cao Jinyuan, the acting principal of Peicheng Girls' School on Xiaoshadu Road, was notified by the Shanghai First Special District Court yesterday upon the request of Lin Peizhen, a teacher at the school, for mediation. Lin Peizhen appointed lawyer Song Yunhui as her representative, and Cao Jinyuan also appointed lawyer He Shimei as her representative. Both parties were represented by their agents. Judge Tao Junde opened the court for mediation, but it failed. It is reported that Lin Peizhen's reasons for requesting mediation were that she was hired to teach at the school last year and received notification from the school this year. However, the school suddenly sent a letter stating that she had written to the school saying that she would not be able to come to school to teach and that another person had been hired to replace her. Lin Peizhen claimed that she did not write such a letter and that she could not be dismissed midway. After repeated negotiations, Cao Jinyuan's attitude was tough, and she even verbally abused Lin Peizhen, so she had no choice but to meet in court. Lin Peizhen is demanding repayment of one month's salary and compensation for damages of six months' salary for the current semester. Since mediation has failed, litigation may be unavoidable, which is an unfortunate event for the education sector.

Letters to the Editor

To the Editor:

I was quite surprised to read a news item entitled "The Dade Steamer Case Resolved" in the local news section of your esteemed newspaper on the 4th of this month. Since the tragic Dade incident occurred on December 13th of last year, Fu Bao has been entrusted by the families concerned to handle the registration matters. While in the process of collecting documents and conducting investigations, the Shanghai Incident occurred, and the matter was suspended. We are now prepared to file a lawsuit with the Shanghai District Court, requesting compensation according to the law. The assertion in your newspaper that the Dada Company has withdrawn tens of thousands of yuan to be distributed to the families is something that Fu Bao and the families he represents have never heard of. We are sincerely concerned that the outside world will not understand the truth, leading to misunderstandings, so we have specially written this letter to clarify matters, hoping that you will make a correction. Respectfully addressed to Mr. Editor of Shenbao, Fu Bao, Lawyer, May 4th.

Dear Editor,

Your esteemed newspaper stated in the local news section on May 3rd that "Dong Manni, a Jiangxi native, was arrested by Chinese detective Cao Qishan of the Laozha Police Station at the intersection of Zhejiang Road and Simalu at 1:10 PM the day before yesterday, shouting reactionary slogans while holding reactionary leaflets. He also had several companions gathering and marching. He confessed that there were more leaflets and books hidden at 76 Avenue du President Haig, French Concession, and 141 Xinxin Lane, Rue du Pere Froc. The police station of the French Concession was notified and the police jointly searched and found quite a lot of reactionary books..." I was extremely astonished after reading this. My family lives at 76 Avenue du President Haig and makes a living by teaching. On May 1st, it is true that a Jiangxi student named Dong Manni was brought to my residence by detectives, who pointed to my residence as his address, but at that time, my family had already clearly denied it. However, the detectives ignored the reasons and went straight upstairs into the house, arbitrarily taking away several volumes of Chinese and foreign books displayed on the bookshelves. Upon investigation, 76 Avenue du President Haig is my residence, and the books are all owned by me. They were not hidden by others and have no connection with Dong Manni. Moreover, all the above-mentioned books, whether in Chinese or foreign languages, are openly and legally published by major bookstores in China or foreign countries. However, your newspaper reported "quite a lot of reactionary books were found," which is clearly an inaccurate report. I respectfully request that you publish this letter, because I am currently pursuing a lawsuit in court, and the word "reactionary" cannot be easily applied to people. With respectful greetings, Li Jianhua, 76 Avenue du President Haig, May 4th.
